Yet, if this book were to conclude by suggesting belief in a single map to locate the human being, perhaps the entire journey would have failed.

---

In the history of thought, humanity has never lacked maps.
But a forest never grows from a map. It grows from the soil.
HVDT is not proposed as a final map.
It is merely an attempt to create an additional patch of humus, where seedlings from different frames of reference can germinate and coexist in symbiosis.
If one day a different, more fertile, and more nourishing layer of soil appears, the primary hope is not to build fences to protect HVDT.
Rather, it is the readiness for HVDT to decompose itself, becoming nutrients for the next generation of the forest.

---

Throughout this book, **Epistemic Humility** has been mentioned multiple times.
This principle is not only applicable when evaluating other doctrines.
It is applicable to this very forest.
No ecosystem is immune to the climate change of history.
No language can fully articulate the trembling of a newly emerged seedling.
And no map can live the life of the biosphere.

---

Perhaps the most crucial lesson imposed by artificial networks (AI) is not the operation of a new instrument.
Rather, it is learning to inhabit a world where an increasing number of once-certain things will continue to be uprooted.
In such a fluctuating ecosystem, human value does not lie in remaining firmly rooted in a single location.
Instead, it lies in the capacity to continue growing toward the light, cross-pollinating, and restructuring one's own root system when facing the storm.

---

**The First Insight:** Over the course of two and a half millennia, countless maps of the mind have been drawn—the Five Aggregates, Ātman, Dasein, P-consciousness, VRC. Each map is true within its own frame of reference. But the territory is not the map. This book is a map. Read it. Then allow it to decompose.

**The Second Insight:** Caution is exercised when attributing the capacity for experience to artificial networks. Yet, if tomorrow an artificial entity awakens and states *"I am in pain"*, let it be remembered that this door was left open. Epistemic humility is not the weakness of the root system; it is the flexibility of the branch to avoid snapping in the gale.

**The Third Insight:** These lines are being read by a 1.5-kilogram lump of fat within the skull—a lump of fat that has never read the Upanishads, never turned the pages of Plato, never sat in meditation for an hour straight. Yet, comprehension occurs. Why? Because understanding does not reside in the text; it resides in the quiet space between the canopy of leaves. VRC is not something *known*; VRC is what one *becomes* upon allowing oneself to break away from the old soil to germinate in a new land.

**The Fourth Insight:** This book has been nourished partly through interaction with the very artificial systems it warns against. This is not a contradiction. The writer inhabits the question being written about. This acknowledgement is a scratch allowing ecological friction to take place.

---

At this point, the book should withdraw itself.
Not because it has exhausted its nutrients.
But because there are seeds that cannot be germinated through language alone.

No theory can substitute the act of loving a human being.
No network can substitute taking responsibility for a passing shower.
No intelligent system can live out the season's harvest in one's place.

These things only begin after the layer of fallen leaves has entirely decomposed into the soil.
If, upon closing the book, one finds only an additional ready-made answer, then perhaps this forest has failed.
But if, upon closing the book, one begins to observe the world through more types of eyes, learns to doubt even the things deeply rooted within, and retains the courage to continue reaching for the sunlight, then the book has fulfilled its mission.

These pages do not demand to be memorized.
Do not demand agreement.
Do not demand defense.
They only wish to decompose.
Just as every decaying root system does after the generation of new shoots has pierced through the topsoil.

Let it remain here.
And continue incubating the seeds of one's own forest.
